# Rekkus — Execution Backlog

`BACKLOG.md` is execution truth. It preserves shipped history, sequences work top-to-bottom, and turns strategy into actionable tasks for humans and AI agents.

Strategic truth: [PRODUCT.md](PRODUCT.md)  
Agent behavior: [AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md)  
AI constraints: [AI_RULES.md](AI_RULES.md)  
Architecture truth: [docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md](docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md)

Status: `[ ]` not started · `[~]` in progress · `[x]` shipped

Lifecycle model: backlog rows use checkbox status for execution state and Implementation Type for delivery shape. Use `[ ]` for not started, `[~]` for actively scoped or partially shipped work, and `[x]` only when implementation evidence exists and related docs/checks are updated. Preserve completed rows as shipped history; reopen with `[~]` when evidence exists but a material gap remains. Docs-only shipping is valid only when the row itself is strategy, owner-index, policy, ADR/template, or intentionally deferred external/legal work; rows that claim validation, automation, runtime behavior, data model support, privacy workflow, media safety, jobs, auditability, or release gating need actual implementation evidence.

## Backlog Column Guide

Backlog section tables use this schema: `| Status | Priority | ID | Item | Why It Matters | Dependencies | Burden | Problem | Suggested AI Command | Implementations | Implementation Type |`

| Column               | What It Must Contain                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| -------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Status               | `[ ]` not started, `[~]` actively scoped or partially shipped, `[x]` shipped with implementation evidence plus docs/checks, or `Deprioritized` for intentionally parked work.                        |
| Priority             | Current execution importance, not long-term strategic ambition.                                                                                                                                      |
| ID                   | Stable backlog reference; never reuse or renumber outside the ordered backlog sequence.                                                                                                              |
| Item                 | Specific deliverable: name the actual system, guardrail, workflow, UI, migration, automation, or doc owner. Avoid vague labels like “setup” or “plan” unless the deliverable really is a plan.       |
| Why It Matters       | Concrete product, compliance, cost, safety, operational, or user-risk reason.                                                                                                                        |
| Dependencies         | Required docs, services, tables, providers, owner actions, or prerequisite decisions.                                                                                                                |
| Burden               | Expected maintenance or operational load: Low, Medium, or High.                                                                                                                                      |
| Problem              | Crisp implementation problem. Include `Compliance Impact:` for risky privacy, provider, security, media, analytics, ranking, auth, payment, moderation, admin, or data changes.                      |
| Suggested AI Command | Actionable `Do:` instruction that says whether to implement code, add a migration, add automation/guardrails, update docs only, or remind Roy about external work. Include verification docs/checks. |
| Implementations      | Shipped evidence with paths/checks, or the exact reason the item is not implemented.                                                                                                                 |
| Implementation Type  | One of `runtime-feature`, `migration`, `guardrail`, `automation`, `ops-workflow`, `docs`, `restructure`, `audit`, `policy`, or `none`.                                                               |

---

## Execution Principles

- Prioritize operational visibility → trust and safety → cost efficiency → release safety → maintainability → product utility → retention → growth loops → advanced discovery → advanced AI systems.
- Build foundational leverage before feature scale: observability, security, caching, release safety, moderation, and data integrity first.
- Keep Google as enrichment, not core serving infrastructure.
- Prefer deterministic systems before AI.
- Preserve completed items for institutional memory.
- Treat the master plan as high-level operating truth and this file as execution truth.

---

| [ ]    | P3       | <a id="b-415"></a>B-415 | Food safety and allergen display readiness        | Health inspection scores, allergen claims, and food safety data create accuracy obligations if Rekkus ever displays them. | Menu management, restaurant data sources, legal review       | Medium | Rekkus should not display health inspection scores, allergen data, or food safety claims until source, timestamp, disclaimer, and correction rules exist. Compliance Impact: food safety/allergen data may involve third-party sources, restaurant-provided claims, timestamps, source links, disclaimers, correction requests, and audit evidence; inaccurate presentation can create user harm and legal risk. | Do: keep food safety/allergen display out of scope until product strategy requires it, then design source/timestamp/disclaimer/correction rules in docs/security/COMPLIANCE.md, product/FEATURES.md, business/RESTAURANT_STRATEGY.md, and BACKLOG.md before implementation. | Not implemented yet; intentionally deferred until Rekkus displays food safety or allergen data.  | none                |
| [ ]    | P3       | <a id="b-416"></a>B-416 | Payments, PCI, Stripe Connect, and AFSL readiness | Payment architecture decisions should be made before Rekkus handles restaurant billing, payouts, or marketplace funds.    | Billing integration, legal/accounting review, provider terms | Medium | Rekkus should use tokenized payment providers and avoid raw card data; Stripe Connect, PCI SAQ A scope, GST/accounting, and AFSL/payment-facilitator risk need review before payments ship. Compliance Impact: payment provider data, billing records, payouts, tax records, store rules, provider DPAs, audit events, and user/restaurant disclosures must be documented before implementation.                 | Do: before billing work starts, document the payment architecture decision, PCI scope, provider terms, payout/legal/accounting risks, and no-raw-card-data rule in business/MONETIZATION.md, docs/security/COMPLIANCE.md, operations/RELEASE.md, and BACKLOG.md.            | Not implemented yet; intentionally deferred until payments or restaurant billing becomes active. | none                |
